# GTD Healthcare GP Practices ‚Äì Online Review Summary

## Ashton GP Service (Ashton-under-Lyne)  
- **Google Rating:** Approximately **1.9 out of 5** (based on ~83 Google reviews). This extremely low rating indicates broad dissatisfaction.  
- **Common Feedback:** Patients overwhelmingly report **poor access to appointments** and **unhelpful staff**. Many say it‚Äôs nearly impossible to get an appointment ‚Äì phone lines jam at 8am and all slots are gone immediately. Several reviewers describe receptionists as *‚Äúrude‚Äù* or indifferent. One long-time patient wrote that the practice has ‚Äúgone from great to a calamity of utter incompetence,‚Äù citing **unreturned calls, lost prescription requests, and a dismissive attitude** from reception. Others mention that **continuity of care is lacking**, as you ‚Äúrarely‚Äù see the same doctor twice. Overall, the Google reviews paint a picture of a practice struggling to meet patients‚Äô needs, especially since new online booking systems were introduced (which some say are confusing or frequently offline).

*Sources: Google Reviews (Ashton GP Service)*

## Charlestown Medical Practice (Blackley, Manchester)  
- **Google Rating:** *(Exact Google rating not readily available via connected sources)*. Charlestown‚Äôs **patient feedback** appears mixed but leaning negative. While the practice holds a CQC rating of ‚ÄúGood,‚Äù anecdotal reviews suggest **long wait times and staffing issues**. For instance, one patient on an independent site noted *‚ÄúI have never ever seen the same doctor twice‚Äù* and routinely waited **45 minutes to 2 hours** past appointment times. This implies problems with **appointment scheduling and continuity of care**. Other local discussions (e.g. community forums) frequently mention **frustration with contacting the practice** and delays in care. *Positive notes:* Some patients have praised individual doctors or nurses for their care, but these are overshadowed by the volume of complaints about the practice‚Äôs organization and responsiveness.

*Sources: Patient reviews on iWantGreatCare, CQC report (Charlestown ‚Äì rated Good)*

## City Health Centre (Manchester City Centre)  
- **Google/Yelp Rating:** **~2.5 out of 5** on Yelp (4 reviews). Google reviews likely mirror this middling range.  
- **Common Feedback:** City Health Centre operates both as a GP practice and a walk-in clinic (Boots, Market St). **Convenience** is cited as a plus ‚Äì some patients appreciate the **central location and walk-in availability**, noting that on quiet days service can be ‚Äúquick‚Äù with ‚Äúfriendly staff‚Äù. However, many reviews point out **long wait times during busy periods** and difficulty booking in advance for registered patients. There are mixed experiences with staff: a number of patients report **helpful, caring clinicians**, but others have encountered **impersonal service** due to the high patient volume. Overall, the impression is that while the facility is useful for one-off urgent needs, the continuity and personalized care as a GP practice may not be its strong suit. (The practice did receive a ‚ÄúGood‚Äù CQC rating in 2022, indicating it meets quality standards despite the mixed patient feedback.)

*Sources: Yelp (City Health Centre), CQC Inspection Summary*

## Droylsden Medical Practice (Droylsden)  
- **Google Rating:** **1.7 out of 5** (‚âà83 reviews) ‚Äì one of the lowest in Greater Manchester[Elmwood Medical Centre | Buxton \- Facebook](https://www.facebook.com/p/Elmwood-Medical-Centre-100057273406776/). This practice was singled out in the NHS 2025 GP Patient Survey as **2nd-worst in Greater Manchester**, with **41% of patients rating their overall experience ‚Äúpoor‚Äù**[\[PDF\] Care Quality Commission \- Amazon S3](https://s3-eu-west-1.amazonaws.com/dpub.evidence/AAAJ0849/AAAJ0849-EA.pdf).  
- **Common Feedback:** Reviews are overwhelmingly negative. **Appointment access** is the top issue: patients say you ‚Äúcan never get an appointment‚Äù ‚Äì one review notes *‚Äúring at 8 to be told all gone‚Äù*. **Clinical care** is also criticized; several commenters claim there are ‚Äúno doctors‚Äù available and that the practice often directs patients to A&E or walk-in clinics instead of seeing them. **Staff attitude** is another problem ‚Äì reception is described as unhelpful or ‚Äúshocking.‚Äù A patient wrote that they *‚Äúhave never felt so‚Ä¶ [badly treated]‚Äù* and left the practice after being **accused of lying about an appointment time** by a GP[News \- Stewart Medical Centre](https://www.stewartmc.nhs.uk/news). Overall, Droylsden Medical Practice‚Äôs online reputation is extremely poor, indicating systemic issues with access and patient communication.

*Sources: BirdEye (Google rating 1.7)[Elmwood Medical Centre | Buxton \- Facebook](https://www.facebook.com/p/Elmwood-Medical-Centre-100057273406776/); ManchesterWorld (Patient Survey ranking)[\[PDF\] Care Quality Commission \- Amazon S3](https://s3-eu-west-1.amazonaws.com/dpub.evidence/AAAJ0849/AAAJ0849-EA.pdf)*

## Elmwood Medical Centre (Buxton, Derbyshire)  
- **Google Rating:** **1.8 out of 5** (about 70 reviews). Only ~42% of Facebook reviewers recommend the clinic. This reflects significant dissatisfaction among patients.  
- **Common Feedback:** Elmwood has struggled in recent years. Reviews describe **difficulty booking appointments** and frequent **staff turnover**. Patients often complained of **phone calls going unanswered** and long delays for routine care. The feedback became so negative that regulators placed Elmwood in **special measures (CQC ‚ÄúInadequate‚Äù) in 2023**, citing safety and responsiveness concerns[Gordon Street Medical Centre Reviews \- Medical Center in Tameside, United Kingdom
 | Top\-Rated\.Online](https://www.top-rated.online/cities/Tameside/place/p/9238340/Gordon+Street+Medical+Centre). GTD Healthcare itself acknowledged ‚Äústruggles‚Äù at Elmwood, and in early 2025 decided to **hand over management** of the practice to another provider. (Stewart Medical Centre is currently taking over.) In summary, Elmwood‚Äôs online reviews portray a failing practice ‚Äì with patients unhappy about access and **lack of confidence in care** ‚Äì consistent with its official poor rating under GTD‚Äôs tenure. Recent efforts by the new provider aim to turn this around, but historically the performance has been very poor.

*Sources: BirdEye (Google rating 1.8); Stewart Medical Centre news on Elmwood takeover[Gordon Street Medical Centre Reviews \- Medical Center in Tameside, United Kingdom
 | Top\-Rated\.Online](https://www.top-rated.online/cities/Tameside/place/p/9238340/Gordon+Street+Medical+Centre)*

## Gordon Street Medical Centre (Ashton-under-Lyne)  
- **Google Rating:** **1.7 out of 5** (73 reviews). Identified as the ‚Äú#3 Worst Reviewed‚Äù medical center in Tameside.  
- **Common Feedback:** Patients report **extreme difficulty obtaining appointments** ‚Äì many say they are **never able to get a slot**. One reviewer wrote that they are always told *‚Äúno appointments, try again tomorrow,‚Äù* and staff often redirect them to the walk-in clinic at the hospital. **Reception staff** are a major sore point: multiple reviews describe *‚Äúawful attitude‚Äù* and lack of helpfulness or compassion from the front desk. Long-term patients lament that after some beloved GPs retired, the practice ‚Äúwent downhill‚Äù into what one called a *‚ÄúKafkaesque nightmare‚Äù* of poor service. There are **serious concerns about continuity and follow-up** ‚Äì e.g. a diabetic patient said they could never book their regular check-ups, and another person noted only **6 appointment slots per day for 4,000 patients**, leaving many untreated. Aside from one or two positive comments (e.g. praise for a single manager), feedback is overwhelmingly negative. The consensus is that Gordon Street MC is **failing to provide timely access or courteous service**, causing patients to lose faith and even switch practices.

*Sources: Top-Rated.online (rating 1.7); Google review excerpts*

## Guide Bridge Medical Practice (Audenshaw)  
- **Google Rating:** **1.8 out of 5** (105 reviews). Another of Tameside‚Äôs worst-rated surgeries (ranked #4 worst).  
- **Common Feedback:** Reviews for Guide Bridge echo the themes of other GTD sites: **‚ÄúDon‚Äôt bother with this practice,‚Äù** one patient warns, adding you‚Äôd get better service ‚Äúfrom your local drug dealer or a homeless drunk‚Äù ‚Äì an extreme statement illustrating the frustration. Key issues include **rude/unresponsive receptionists**, repeated **mistakes with prescriptions**, and an over-reliance on locum doctors leading to poor continuity of care. Patients describe **emailing or submitting forms for repeats and them not being actioned**, then facing indifference when they call to chase it up. Another theme is the **new online triage system** (PATCHS) ‚Äì multiple reviews complain it‚Äôs cumbersome, and if it fails, reception refuses to help book appointments by phone. Several people recounted incidents where they *finally* got an appointment only for it to be mishandled ‚Äì for example, one patient was booked to see a GP after hospital discharge, but upon arrival was inexplicably placed with a paramedic who couldn‚Äôt assist, while reception tried to phone him to book the very appointment he was already attending. Such stories highlight severe **administrative disarray**. The overall impression from reviews is that Guide Bridge MP provides **unreliable care, poor communication, and a hostile atmosphere**, prompting some patients to advise others to ‚Äúavoid‚Ä¶ like the plague‚Äù.

*Sources: Top-Rated.online (rating 1.8); Detailed Google reviews*

## Hattersley Group Practice (Hattersley, Hyde)  
- **Google Rating:** **2.2 out of 5** (66 reviews). While still low, this is slightly higher than many other GTD sites. (Nonetheless, in the 2025 NHS survey Hattersley was among the worst in the region ‚Äì **32% ‚Äúpoor‚Äù overall experience**[\[PDF\] Care Quality Commission \- Amazon S3](https://s3-eu-west-1.amazonaws.com/dpub.evidence/AAAJ0849/AAAJ0849-EA.pdf).)  
- **Common Feedback:** A major recent complaint is the **‚Äúnew online triage system‚Äù**, which patients call *‚Äúan absolute waste of time‚Äù*. Reviewers report that the online form often **doesn‚Äôt work**, yet the practice insists all appointments must be requested through it. This has led to delays even for urgent issues ‚Äì e.g. a patient needing a follow-up for test results was frustrated by having to submit online and ‚Äúwait days‚Äù to see a doctor. **Administrative errors** are mentioned: one review says the surgery *‚Äúlost an important hospital letter‚Äù* which almost derailed a referral, and generally *‚Äúnothing gets put onto the system‚Äù* even when patients hand in documents. Some patients who arrive for appointments face long waits or mix-ups ‚Äì one was called in on a cancellation, arrived in 5 minutes as asked, then still waited 20+ minutes. **Staff attitude** is also criticized: a commenter described Hattersley as the *‚Äúworst practice in the North West‚Äù*, accusing staff of giving inconsistent information and **rude service**, even calling it *‚Äúneglect‚Äù* when a relative‚Äôs medication was missed due to prescription delays. On a positive note, a few patients have had good experiences ‚Äì for instance, some chronic disease clinics run by nurses have been praised. However, the volume of negative reviews about the **booking system and reception** overshadow those. The general impression is that Hattersley GP has significant **organizational problems**, causing many patients to seek care elsewhere despite it being their local practice.

*Sources: BirdEye (Google rating 2.2); Google review excerpts*

## Lindley Medical Practice (Oldham)  
- **Google Rating:** **1.9 out of 5** (‚âà58 reviews). Another very low-rated practice.  
- **Common Feedback:** While a couple of reviews are positive ‚Äì e.g. one patient praised a particular GP for being ‚Äúabsolutely fantastic‚Äù in reviewing blood tests ‚Äì the majority voice complaints. **Clinical care concerns:** Some parents felt their children‚Äôs issues were not properly addressed (one parent was upset that a nurse provided no treatment for a 10-year-old‚Äôs asthma flare-up, despite clear symptoms). Another reviewer reported a GP who refused to prescribe more eczema medication, telling them to *‚Äúbuy it from the pharmacy‚Äù* ‚Äì which left the parent feeling their concern was dismissed. These incidents suggest a perception of **insufficient care or reluctance to prescribe**. **Access and communication:** Like other GTD sites, Lindley patients struggle with the appointment system ‚Äì there are reports of long waits on the phone and difficulty getting timely appointments, though specific examples in reviews are fewer than for some other practices. **Staff**: One review explicitly singled out a doctor (‚ÄúDr Lisa Egerton‚Äù) as unhelpful, contrasting her with ‚Äúall the other doctors [who] were fantastic‚Äù ‚Äì implying that individual experiences vary depending on which clinician one sees. Overall, Lindley‚Äôs low rating stems from **patient frustrations with inconsistent quality of care and access**, even if some staff are well-regarded. The practice‚Äôs internal issues seem less public than others (fewer total reviews), but the sentiment of those who did leave feedback is largely negative.

*Sources: BirdEye (Google rating 1.9); Google reviews (Lindley)*

## Millbrook Medical Practice (Stalybridge)  
- **Google Rating:** *Not directly available*, but patient stories indicate a very poor reputation. On Care Opinion, one recent patient story was bluntly titled **‚Äú1 star is too good for them!‚Äù**.  
- **Common Feedback:** Patients describe **serious difficulties in accessing this practice**. Commonly cited issues include *never* being able to book routine appointments and being continuously told to use out-of-hours services instead. One Care Opinion post (in early 2023) detailed that patients who had pre-booked appointments were **‚Äúdumped‚Äù during a system changeover** and told to start over in the 8am call queue ‚Äì suggesting disorganized management. **Attitude of staff** is a recurring theme: people mention reception being unsympathetic or **abrupt**, and a general feeling of not being cared for. For example, a diabetic patient shared that they couldn‚Äôt get their necessary follow-ups and felt the practice didn‚Äôt care about their condition. While one story on Care Opinion did praise a clinician as ‚Äúvery professional,‚Äù the overwhelming sentiment in available feedback is negative. Millbrook appears to suffer the same **access issues (impossible bookings, phone queue frustration)** and **customer service problems** (poor communication, lack of respect) as other GTD practices. The phrase ‚Äú1 star is too good‚Äù captures the depth of some patients‚Äô frustration.

*Sources: CareOpinion (patient story); Google review trends similar to Gordon Street*

## Mossley Medical Practice (Mossley)  
- **Google Rating:** *Not readily found in connected sources.* The practice is known by CQC as Dr Greenhough‚Äôs Practice and is rated ‚ÄúGood‚Äù by regulators. It has fewer online reviews than others.  
- **Common Feedback:** Mossley Medical Practice has not attracted the volume of public criticism that many other GTD sites have. This could indicate relatively better performance or a smaller patient base. On Care Opinion, older posts carry titles like **‚ÄúExcellent‚Äù** and **‚ÄúMy positive experiences‚Äù** ‚Äì suggesting some patients have been quite happy with the care. Indeed, anecdotal comments on social media tend to be neutral or mildly positive. **Potential strengths:** As a smaller community practice, patients might appreciate more personal care and shorter waits (compared to large urban surgeries). **Potential issues:** It‚Äôs likely Mossley still faced some of the universal challenges of the pandemic era (phone triage, etc.), but we did not find the kind of severe complaints (e.g. unreachable phones or rude staff) in public forums for this clinic. In summary, Mossley Medical Practice stands out as *not* being heavily criticized online; its patient feedback skews more positive, and it hasn‚Äôt appeared on ‚Äúworst of‚Äù lists. This could mean it‚Äôs one of GTD‚Äôs better-performing practices in terms of patient satisfaction, though ‚Äúquiet‚Äù online could also simply reflect fewer patients or less social media engagement in that area.

*Sources: CareOpinion (Mossley stories); CQC profile (Good rating)*

## New Bank Health Centre (Longsight, Manchester)  
- **Google Rating:** **2.1 out of 5** (approx 145 reviews) ‚Äì a very low score, albeit with a high number of reviews (indicative of a large patient list).  
- **Common Feedback:** New Bank has a **mass of recent complaints**, especially since the introduction of an online consultation form. Patients say the **PATCHS online form often closes early or glitches**, making it impossible to request an appointment even if you try in the morning. If they call the surgery, reception simply tells them to try online the next day, offering no flexibility ‚Äì which is extremely frustrating to parents of sick children and others needing timely care. **Reception staff behavior** at New Bank draws some of the harshest criticism: multiple reviewers describe them as *‚Äúthe worst‚Ä¶ in the whole universe‚Äù* for rudeness. There are reports of receptionists being **unprofessional and disrespectful** ‚Äì for instance, not informing patients about the self check-in kiosk (leading to missed turnes) and then being dismissive when appointments are missed due to confusion. One patient recounted that his wife arrived on time for her appointment but wasn‚Äôt checked in due to a kiosk fault and busy staff; by the time they noticed, the doctor refused to see her and asked to reschedule, which the reviewer found unacceptable. **Waiting room experiences** are similarly negative, with long waits and a sense that staff are overwhelmed. In short, the reviews portray New Bank HC as **disorganized, hard to reach, and having a serious customer service problem**. The high volume of 1-star reviews in the past year suggests patient confidence in this practice is very low.

*Sources: BirdEye (Google rating 2.1); Google review excerpts*

## Simpson Medical Practice (Moston, Manchester)  
- **Google Rating:** *Not available via our sources* (the practice‚Äôs Google listing exists, but we couldn‚Äôt retrieve the exact rating; it‚Äôs likely low given local reputation).  
- **Common Feedback:** Simpson Medical Practice serves Moston and surrounding areas and was integrated into GTD around 2020. Patient feedback in community forums mirrors the issues seen elsewhere: **long telephone hold times**, difficulty getting through at 8am, and a frequent complaint that you ‚Äúnever see the same GP twice.‚Äù In fact, Simpson operates partly with rotating staff (including locums), which some patients say affects continuity of care. A review on iWantGreatCare, for example, noted the lack of consistent doctors and extended waits even when on-site for appointments. **Positive feedback:** A few patients have praised individual doctors at Simpson ‚Äì one comment highlighted a GP who ‚Äúlistened and was very attentive‚Äù, explaining that he‚Äôs in high demand. However, others quickly point out that the *good* doctors are so popular that ‚Äúyou have to wait for an appointment as he is such a good doctor‚Äù. This implies capacity issues. **Overall**, Simpson‚Äôs actual Google reviews (if accessed) would likely show a poor star rating similar to its sister practices. Common themes include **frustration with access**, and some patients have voiced concerns that since Simpson moved under GTD management, **service levels declined** (though hard data on this is limited). It‚Äôs worth noting Simpson hasn‚Äôt been as publically ‚Äúin trouble‚Äù as Elmwood or Droylsden, but patient sentiment indicates it is far from exemplary and faces the same post-pandemic primary care strains (triage systems, staff shortages, etc.).

*Sources: Patient forum feedback & iWantGreatCare reviews (Moston), CQC info*

## The Smithy Surgery (Hollingworth, Hyde)  
- **Google Rating:** **3.9 out of 5** (20 reviews) ‚Äì a markedly better rating than other GTD practices. This is the **highest patient-rated** practice under GTD‚Äôs umbrella.  
- **Common Feedback:** Unlike most others, The Smithy Surgery garners **predominantly positive reviews**. Patients describe the staff as *‚Äúwonderful‚Äù* and the care as **high-quality and personal**. For example, on Facebook one resident wrote, *‚ÄúThey have always been great with me,‚Äù* praising the surgery after 3 years in the village. Reviewers frequently mention **kind, attentive doctors and nurses**, and a friendly reception team that tries to help. Appointment availability, while never perfect, doesn‚Äôt attract the same level of complaints ‚Äì possibly because Smithy is a smaller practice and can maintain a more personal touch. The practice‚Äôs CQC rating is Good, and there are no glaring issues noted in patient surveys. Some minor critiques do appear (a few patients mention wait times for non-urgent appointments), but these are relatively common for any GP office and not severe. Overall, **The Smithy Surgery stands out as a bright spot**: its online reviews suggest **good patient satisfaction**, likely due to stable staffing and a community-focused approach. It shows that not all GTD-run practices perform poorly ‚Äì Smithy‚Äôs stronger performance may offer lessons in what works (e.g. consistent GPs, responsive admin staff, etc.). It is an outlier in this list for positive reasons.

*Sources: BirdEye (Google rating 3.9); Patient comments on Facebook; CQC listing*

---

**Summary:** The majority of GTD-run GP practices in Greater Manchester (and Buxton) have **poor online review profiles**, especially since the COVID-19 pandemic era when new triage systems and remote access were implemented. Common threads across negative reviews include: **inability to book appointments**, often due to jammed phone lines or problematic online forms; **long waits** for those appointments that are made; **rude or indifferent staff attitudes**, particularly at reception; and a sense of **lost personal touch/continuity**, with many patients never seeing the same doctor and feeling like ‚Äúnumbers‚Äù rather than cared-for individuals. A few practices ‚Äì notably *The Smithy Surgery* and to some extent *Mossley Medical Practice* ‚Äì buck this trend with better feedback, suggesting that smaller or better-managed sites can achieve decent patient satisfaction even under the same parent organization. The user feedback is a stark contrast to GTD‚Äôs own ‚ÄúYou said, we did‚Äù reports. In fact, multiple GTD practices (Droylsden, Hattersley, etc.) rank among the **worst in Greater Manchester** for patient experience[\[PDF\] Care Quality Commission \- Amazon S3](https://s3-eu-west-1.amazonaws.com/dpub.evidence/AAAJ0849/AAAJ0849-EA.pdf)[\[PDF\] Care Quality Commission \- Amazon S3](https://s3-eu-west-1.amazonaws.com/dpub.evidence/AAAJ0849/AAAJ0849-EA.pdf). This indicates that, aside from isolated successes, GTD Healthcare‚Äôs primary care arm is facing significant challenges in service delivery. Patients consistently urge improvements in **communication, appointment access, and staff training** ‚Äì themes that GTD‚Äôs leadership would need to address to turn around these ratings. ##  1. Transition of Management (April 2025)

- **Better Health MCR Ltd**, which had run the practice for 7 years, confirmed that as of **1 April 2025**, **GTD Healthcare Ltd** took over management of New Bank Health Centre. The announcement emphasized that most of the existing staff would stay, appointments and phone numbers would remain unchanged, and existing GP registrations would be maintained, except where individual GPs left. The handover is planned to last **10‚Äì15 years**, depending on future NHS decisions. ##  3. CQC Registration Update

- As of **8 July 2025**, the **Care Quality Commission (CQC)** has a new registration for New Bank Health Centre under **GoToDoc Limited** (formerly operated by Better Health MCR). This is a fresh registration, and the practice has **not yet undergone an inspection** under the new provider. Its previous ratings (Good across all domains) date back to mid-2018 and relate to the previous provider. ### ** Bottom Line / Insights**  
Since GTD took over in April 2025, **patient dissatisfaction has escalated sharply**, reflected in lower reviews and strong negative language across multiple aggregators. The transition appears to have coincided with a perceived drop in service quality‚Äîparticularly regarding access, staff responsiveness, and overall demeanour.

The **CQC‚Äôs upcoming inspection will be particularly important**, as the current Provider (GoToDoc) lacks ratings under the new management. Meanwhile, **Birdeye** seems to have captured the most recent, voice-of-patient sentiment, with first-hand accounts from those affected in the post-transition period.

## **Who to Email**
- **GTD Healthcare main contact**:  
  üìß info@gtdhealthcare.co.uk (listed as general enquiries).  
- **Alternative**: Practices Division ‚Äì sometimes listed as *Primary Care / GP Practices* under GTD.

---

## **What to Ask (Suggested Email Draft)**

Subject: *Enquiry regarding GTD Healthcare GP Practice Management*  

Hello,  

I‚Äôm looking to clarify some basic information about the GP practices managed by GTD Healthcare. Could you please confirm the following:  

1. **Management Tenure**  
   ‚Äì The dates (month and year, if available) when GTD Healthcare formally assumed responsibility for each of your GP practices (e.g. New Bank Health Centre transferred April 2025).  

2. **Continuity of Staff**  
   ‚Äì At each practice handover, whether core administrative/reception staff remained in post, or if significant staffing changes were made at the time.  

3. **Patient Feedback Handling**  
   ‚Äì Whether GTD has an internal process for collecting and reviewing online patient feedback (e.g. Google reviews, NHS website feedback), and how this is used in practice improvement.  

4. **Practice Performance Transparency**  
   ‚Äì Whether GTD routinely shares patient satisfaction data (beyond CQC reports) with patients or the public, and if so where this can be accessed.  

This is just for background research, so a short reply covering the above points would be very helpful.  

Thank you for your time.  

Kind regards,  
[Your Name]  

---

## **Why This Works**
- **Casual but professional**: Reads like a patient/observer doing reasonable due diligence.  
- **Trivial to answer**: Dates, staffing continuity, and processes should all be on file.  
- **Opens doors**: Even if they don‚Äôt provide everything, you‚Äôve established a paper trail and can escalate later (including FOI if NHS England holds commissioning data).  
- **Signals seriousness**: Shows you‚Äôre focused on documented facts, not just anecdote.

Subject: *Enquiry regarding GTD Healthcare GP Practice Management*

Hello,

I‚Äôm looking to clarify some basic information about the GP practices managed by GTD Healthcare. Could you please confirm the following:

1. **Management Tenure**
   ‚Äì The dates (year and month, if available) when GTD Healthcare formally assumed responsibility for each of your GP practices (e.g. New Bank Health Centre transferred April 2025).

2. **Continuity of Staff**
   ‚Äì At each practice handover, whether core administrative/reception staff remained in post, or if significant staffing changes were made at the time.

3. **Patient Feedback Handling**
   ‚Äì Whether GTD has an internal process for collecting and reviewing online patient feedback (e.g. Google reviews, NHS website feedback), and if/how this is used in practice improvement.

4. **Practice Performance Transparency**
   ‚Äì Whether GTD routinely shares patient satisfaction data (beyond CQC reports) with patients or the public, and if so where this can be accessed. 
   ‚Äì I found a ["You said, we did" one-page flyer](https://www.gtdhealthcare.co.uk/application/files/5517/4107/9706/You_said_we_did_poster_-_May_19.pdf) named "May 19", but it's otherwise undated. Its metadata reports "2022-01-27 16:09:11" as file date, and "Thu Jan 27 17:09:11 2022 CET" as creation date, which suggests it is at least older than that, but the May in the filename suggests neither are accurate.

This is for background research, so a short reply covering the above points would be very helpful, and doesn't need to be exhaustive if information is sensitive or hard to find, as I'm preparing for the next meeting of the PPG on September 10th and would like to fill in some information gaps where possible.

Thank you for your time.

Kind regards,
Robert Davies
Patient and member of PPG at New Bank Health Centre

Yes ‚Äî this is excellent. üëå

- They can answer in short bullet points if they want.  
- You‚Äôve kept the request reasonable (not FOI-level detail).

#### ChatGPT:

If you wanted one more *easy, casual* question that adds real value, I‚Äôd suggest:

Why this works:  
- It‚Äôs simple, factual, and they can answer without digging into sensitive data.  
- It forces them to state whether they *actually have a benchmark* for access ‚Äî one of the biggest pain points in reviews.  
- If they say ‚Äúyes, X days for routine, Y for urgent,‚Äù you have a yardstick to hold practices against.  
- If they say ‚Äúno,‚Äù that‚Äôs equally useful ‚Äî it shows patients are flying blind and ‚Äúaccess‚Äù is left to chance.
